  <span id="freeText4943456835227607964" style="display:none">literally all i want to do right now is lie facedown on the ground and contemplate over what the actual fuckhell i did to deserve this. @god say it to my face bitch<br /><br />every time i read a terrible book i feel like i'm being fucked over twice, because not only do i have to 1) read the damn thing, i also have to 2) review it and go through the whole disaster again. good thing i've been practicing burning self-hatred for 20 years now in order to prepare myself for situations like this 🤠👉🏼<br /><br />i don't think you have any idea how much it actually pains me to look at my own rating. it breaks my little heart into a million tiny pieces.<br />i read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41014903.Warcross__Warcross___1_" title="Warcross (Warcross, #1) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">warcross</a> back in january, and it became an instant favorite. i remember it being so addictive, so easy to read. it was the thing that my inner nerd desired. and it was what she deserved.<br /> <br /><b>and now i can't even correlate <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41014903.Warcross__Warcross___1_" title="Warcross (Warcross, #1) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">warcross</a> with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22587069.Wildcard_Volume_One__Wildcard___1_" title="Wildcard Volume One (Wildcard, #1) by Missy Johnson" rel="nofollow noopener">wildcard</a>, like someone tell me why these books seem to take place in two entirely disparate universes??</b><br /><br /><u>
  <blockquote>but, let me start at the beginning:</blockquote>
</u><br />the core, the whole idea of warcross, to me, was brilliant. it was exciting and thrilling and absolutely terrifying: <i>virtual reality advancing even farther than we can imagine in this day and age</i>. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4342215.Marie_Lu" title="Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">marie lu</a> created something that i loved. the warcross matches were the first thing that i could compare to quidditch in terms of "oh my god i love this i want to be a part of this please give me 398 pages of only this". and that was where i went wrong. apparently.<br /><br />because <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4342215.Marie_Lu" title="Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener"> marie lu</a> had a completely different idea for the series. the original idea of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41014903.Warcross__Warcross___1_" title="Warcross (Warcross, #1) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">warcross</a> slowly perished under whatever it is that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22587069.Wildcard_Volume_One__Wildcard___1_" title="Wildcard Volume One (Wildcard, #1) by Missy Johnson" rel="nofollow noopener">wildcard</a> was trying to be. she felt the need to turn it into something that i couldn't identify anymore.<br /><br />and this is where i have to put my <b>!!!!!!!!! SPOILER WARNING !!!!!!!!!</b><br /><br /><u>i'm about to get real petty so i suggest you better RUN (all the issues i had with this book: in notes):</u><br /><br /><blockquote>• this went from the idea of a VR world to an AI trying to take over humanity, somehow<br />• ummm???<br />• literally nobody asked for this<br />• can i just enjoy my fighting robot dragons in peace<br />• i feel like a lot of the actions that were happening didn't even make sense<br />• marie lu was literally just throwing plot twist after plot twist at us, trying to make something great out of something that was already enough. and ruined it with that<br />• please all i want is one goddamn game of warcross.... isn't that what i signed up for?<br />• stop the redemption arc trope i'm begging to all gods<br />• emika going back to hideo (a #confirmed murderer) literally gave me the fucking rest<br />• ????????? NO SERIOUSLY IS NOBODY GOING TO TALK ABOUT THAT<br />• HE MIND CONTROLLED THE WHOLE ENTIRE WORLD??? and when confronted with that he was legit like "y'all hear sum?"<br />• at least feel a LITTLe bit bad about yourself <br />• did anybody even really like hideo? genuine question<br />• is hideo short for hideous<br />• emika was so stale in this whole entire thing really<br />• i was bored during a solid 20% of the book. which doesn't sound like a lot but BOI IT IS i tried so hard not to skim<br />• where are my team dynamics? i literally only asked for one (1) thing<br />• not enough Asher<br />• again: the original idea of the warcross games literally went out the window<br />• do i even have to talk about Zero<br />• god i'm so pissed<br />• at least make it gayer <br />• everything is messy messy messy i have a headache just thinking about the last 100 pages<br />• why<br />• god why<br />• it felt like marie lu had some good ideas but she didn't execute them well enough<br />• and all at once<br />• nothing made sense</blockquote><br /><br />and that's that on that, folks. the sad thing? i actually really liked the first half of the book. and i was so ready to love this book with all of my shriveled up tired soul.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22587069.Wildcard_Volume_One__Wildcard___1_" title="Wildcard Volume One (Wildcard, #1) by Missy Johnson" rel="nofollow noopener">wildcard</a> ruined <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41014903.Warcross__Warcross___1_" title="Warcross (Warcross, #1) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">warcross</a> for me. and that's the tea for today! thanks for tuning in.<br /><br /><blockquote><b>⦁ buddy read</b> with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/49148508-may" rel="nofollow noopener">miss may</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/10502567-jiana" rel="nofollow noopener">gianna</a> &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/36873117-maram" rel="nofollow noopener">marami</a></blockquote></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2196628105" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer2240792479775418402">Warcross: ★★★★☆ <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2124754005?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>my review</a><br/>Wildcard : ★★★★☆<br/><br/><b>SPOILER-FREE REVIEW</b><br/><br/><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote><br/>When the world is murky, guide yourself with your own steady light.<br/></blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br/><br/>Finally! I can review this book, I was busy with college assignments and I even barely had time to read, but thankfully I've done mostly all of my assignments and I'm a bit free! YAY! But I'm going to have final exams in a few weeks, so maybe I'll get inactive when I have my final exams but I'll be back again! :)<br/><br/><b>
  <u>My opinion time!</u>
</b><br/><br/>I read Warcross a year ago </span>
  <span id="freeText2240792479775418402" style="display:none">Warcross: ★★★★☆ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2124754005?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">my review</a><br />Wildcard : ★★★★☆<br /><br /><b>SPOILER-FREE REVIEW</b><br /><br /><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote><br />When the world is murky, guide yourself with your own steady light.<br /></blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br /><br />Finally! I can review this book, I was busy with college assignments and I even barely had time to read, but thankfully I've done mostly all of my assignments and I'm a bit free! YAY! But I'm going to have final exams in a few weeks, so maybe I'll get inactive when I have my final exams but I'll be back again! :)<br /><br /><b>
  <u>My opinion time!</u>
</b><br /><br />I read Warcross a year ago and omg that book was really good. It was action-packed and then the world, the technology, basically everything in Warcross was very good and it also hit a little bit close to home for me. I shed a few tears. Warcross was a great read for me. <br /><br />I swear I was so nervous and afraid when I read Wildcard because I really liked Warcross and I was afraid that this book would disappointed me because usually when I have high expectations of a book, then the book let me down later on. However, that did not happen to me with this book. Well, yeah the book was pretty slow at first but it never bored me and I always agreed with Emika. Like I don't even know how that's even possible that I agreed with her with every of her decisions.<br /><br />Emika was such a strong and fierce character and it was always easy for me to like her. Emika was not the only great character in this book, the other characters were also great and they even made me laugh and the friendship in this book was honestly so sweet! they supported each other and helped each other. To be honest, I even felt a twinge of jealousy because I also want to have this kind of friendship in my real life. *sighs* <br /><br />and there was this certain characters ( I'm not gonna tell you you who this character was because it would be a spoiler, if did tell you ) So this certain character caused me pain. Like so much pain, my eyes got really teary and I couldn't hold back my tears anymore and the only thing I wanted do was to hold this character and sob. <br /><br />JUST READ THE BOOK PLEASE <br /><br />and OH MY GOD this book! this book messed with my mind. There were moments where I just clutched my hair and read the book as fast as possible because I needed to know what's next and next and there was also a moment where I just felt like my heart was cracking slowly and my eyes were teary and I was so sad. This book made me feel a lot of emotions, happy, sad, relieved, anger and many more. Wow. I really liked this book. <br /><br />Wildcard was good but I also feel that it was not as good as Warcross. I mean Warcross was a pretty fun read for me but Wildcard was darker than what I expected and I liked it but ... I don't know there's something that I cannot explain because I don't even know it myself but for me Warcross was slightly better than Wildcard. But Wildcard was still good though. It was such good read for me. <br /><br />Thank you very much for reading and liking this review. I appreciate it so much guys and I hope you all have an amazing day! ❤❤<br /><br /><br />•••••••••••••••••••••••••••••••••••••••••••••<br /><br /><s>
  <b>REVIEW TO COME ON SUNDAY!</b>
</s><br /><br />•••••••••••••••••••••••••••••••••••••••••••••<br /><br /><b>
  <s>I'm currently reading this book, which I've been so excited and curious about since I finished reading Warcross. I AM SO READY TO FEEL ALL THE EMOTIONS. AHHHH. Please don't disappoint me book! <br /><br />I also have a crush on Hideo! He's so 😍💓 honestly where can I find a guy like him in my real life? Lol 😂<br /><br /></s>
</b></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1670198794?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hillary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hillary" href="/user/show/18999155-hillary">Hillary</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399547997" href="/book/show/39508596-wildcard">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18999155-hillary?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18999155-hillary?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1670198794" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8578962451949795436">4.5 stars<br/><br/>I am deceased. <br/>If you see me cry it’s not because of this book or that ending. Nope.<br/><br/>What a ride. This conclusion was really different from the first book and I didn't mind at all. Welcome unpredictable, fast-paced and action-packed narrative, and welcome to my new attraction to Zero.<br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>He leans back against the wall, his arms crossed casually over his chest, one of his leg propped against the other. His face is no longer hidden behind a black helmet, and instead of his armor, he's weari</blockquote></i></span>
  <span id="freeText8578962451949795436" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br><br>I am deceased. <br>If you see me cry it’s not because of this book or that ending. Nope.<br><br>What a ride. This conclusion was really different from the first book and I didn't mind at all. Welcome unpredictable, fast-paced and action-packed narrative, and welcome to my new attraction to Zero.<br><br><i>
  <blockquote>He leans back against the wall, his arms crossed casually over his chest, one of his leg propped against the other. His face is no longer hidden behind a black helmet, and instead of his armor, he's wearing a simple black sweater and dark pants, his shoes polished to a shine. But his mannerisms are unmistakable to me.<br>One side of his mouth tilts up in a smile. "Well, Emika," says Zero. "Welcome."</blockquote>
</i><br><br>This was his book, it's as simple as that. And all the twists and turns made me care about him more and more. I could say I like him almost as much as I like Hideo but I guess that's not possible, right? Hideo is... *sighs* Every time he was mentioned I fangirled. <br>That yacht scene? The feels! And that's why I'm still single.<br><br><i>
  <blockquote>I think back to the piercing gaze he’d given me during our last meeting. Underneath that had been fear, all along. “You told me you never wanted to see me again,” I manage to say.<br>His voice is low and raw. “Because every time I see you, it takes everything in me to turn away.”</blockquote>
</i><br><br>I loved the plot of this book more than the first one! Warcross was more predictable because of the championships, but this one strays totally away from them and gives attention to what is actually the duology core conflict. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I think my favorite part was when Jax (who I love btw) shows Zero's memories to Emika and pieces finally start to come together. That was seriously heartbreaking. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>How will I cope without a new book in this series? How will I cope without Hideo?<br><br>————<br><br><b>Update #9</b><br><br>*DEAD*<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1533755629i/26097227._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1535737630i/26231250._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>Update #8</b><br><br>WELL.<br>FUCK.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1532548366i/26028119._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>Update #7</b><br><br>You know you’re trash for a character when you read a simple quote of them talking for about 3 seconds and you squeal like you’ve just been gifted a ticket to the Wizarding World of Harry Potter.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1530862951i/25930774._SY540_.png" alt="4425_DDA6-6843-4974-85_F5-5_AD6_A9_F3_DDDC" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>Update #6</b> <br><br>ARE YOU HEARING ME SCREAM????????!!!!<br>MY BTS BIAS IS IN MY MOST ANTICIPATED BOOK EVER AND I’M SLOWLY DYINGGGG<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1530168578i/25873200._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>Update #5</b><br><br>That moment when you see all these people with Wildcard arcs and you die a little inside.<br><br><br><b>Update #4</b><br><br>I admit I was confused at first and didn’t really like the cover. But as it happened with the Warcross one, after looking at it for a bit I’m seriously so happy about this cover! I guess both covers just are not my style but I can see where they’re coming from and I appreciate them so much.<br>This cover totally <b>SCREAMS HIDEO</b> and I’m HERE FOR IT!!!<br>(It probably also refers to Zero but this girl is blind when it comes to this series and can only see Hideo everywhere. Sorry not sorry)<br><br><br><b>Update #3</b><br><br>THIS IS NOT A DRILL. <br>COVER REVEAL ON MONDAY!!!!!<br>YAAAASSSSS<br><br><br><b>Update #2</b><br><br>O<br>M<br>G<br><br>THIS TITLE IS EVERYTHING <br>I LOVE IT<br>I CAN’T<br><br>I don’t know why I’m hyperventilating because it’s so simple and I don’t understand why I didn’t think about it in the first place, but I am. Hyperventilating I mean.<br>Wake me up when we have a cover. Or on September 18. Because the wait will kill me if I think too much about how badly I want to read this book right now. <br><br><br><b>Update #1</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1521965643i/25270986._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Definitely a title!! I can’t guess so I’m waiting for the reveal tomorrow :D<br>GameOver would be AMAZING tho. <br><br><br><b>Update #0</b><br><br>OMGGGGG I’M SCREAMING!!!<br>IS IT MONDAY YET?? I WANT TO KNOW WHAT WE GET! Title? Official publication date?? Cover???<br>I’M DEAD.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1521621606i/25249136._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_2958284005" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2958284005" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2958284005?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=ya-series">ya-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2958284005" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10727653794900030221"><blockquote> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1576421474i/28616265._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><i>That's the difference between the real and the virtual. Reality is where you can lose the ones you love. Reality is the place where you can feel the cracks in your heart.</i>
</blockquote>Oh. Good. Lawd. What is wrong with her???<br/><br/>To recap -<b> rainbow-haired-tumblr-queen</b> Emika Chen (also hacker-extraordinaire, brilliant strategist, adorably naive in just the right ways) discovered that the guy she's had a crush on (Hideo - <b>dark-haired, emotionally underdeveloped, walking emo stereotype</b>) is actually pretty d*mn evi</span>
  <span id="freeText10727653794900030221" style="display:none"><blockquote> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1576421474i/28616265._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><i>That's the difference between the real and the virtual. Reality is where you can lose the ones you love. Reality is the place where you can feel the cracks in your heart.</i>
</blockquote>Oh. Good. Lawd. What is wrong with her???<br><br>To recap -<b> rainbow-haired-tumblr-queen</b> Emika Chen (also hacker-extraordinaire, brilliant strategist, adorably naive in just the right ways) discovered that the guy she's had a crush on (Hideo - <b>dark-haired, emotionally underdeveloped, walking emo stereotype</b>) is actually pretty d*mn evil.<br><br>He's created a new (and sinister) algorithm for his NeuroLink (think Virtual Reality but connected to your brain...yeah...worked out just the way you'd expect).<br><br>And this new algorithm <b><i>conveniently</i> takes over the entire world</b> (at least everyone with a NeuorLink) and prevents them from being criminals. <blockquote>
  <i>Every problem has a solution. But after every solution, there's a new problem to tackle, some new challenge to take on. </i>
</blockquote> Hideo hides behind <b>a paper-thin moral shield </b>- ohhhh no Emika, I just want to make the world safer - and, like an idiot, Emika returns to his side over and over.<blockquote>
  <i>The mind can make you believe whatever it wants you to believe.</i>
</blockquote>Ultimately...we realize there are betrayals around every corner, what seemed black-and-white is actually grey, yadda yadda yadda. <blockquote>
  <i>“Am I ever going to see you again?" Hideo asks him. In his voice is his lost self, the boy who grew up with a silver streak of grief in his hair.</i>
</blockquote>Annnnnyway, if you can't already tell...in the terms of hit or miss...this one was a miss. A HUGE miss.<br><br>It was so FRUSTRATING.<br><br>No matter the <b>strange deaths</b> associated with this algorithm - or the complete erasure of free will - Emika's raven-haired prince is super cute, so she decided to <b>just swipe all that under the metaphorical rug.</b><br><br>We run around a lot in this book - someone wants to kill Emika for being too cool (read: overpowered) so we get a Scooby-Doo escque plot. <br><br>And the other major thing was Emika constantly trying o convert Hideo back to the "good" side (though, if you're asking me...she really is not taking this murderous side of him seriously). <br><br>I really just couldn't get over....well....a lot of things.<br><br>Emika<b> trusted everyone too much,</b> which led to some pretty expected betrayals.<br><br>Hideo was<b> pretty dang evil</b>, but got away with it because he was pretty.<br><br>The big reveal required literal chapters to explain and was more of a burden to piece together than an aha moment. <br><br>All in all - I can't believe that I'm never going to get this time back.<br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!</span>

<div id="review_2538115793" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2538115793" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2538115793?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2538115793" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12186112909476519594">I'm between 4 and 4.5 stars.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>Wildcard</i>
</b> represents the third series of Marie Lu's I've read to completion, and once again, I am amazed at her talent at building complex, compelling settings and creating characters you empathize with (as well as some you root against). Sure, sometimes the plots get a little bit technical or complicated, but at their core, Lu's books are about human connection, and we can all use a little more of that.<br/><br/>"When the world is murky, guide yourself with your own steady </span>
  <span id="freeText12186112909476519594" style="display:none">I'm between 4 and 4.5 stars.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Wildcard</i>
</b> represents the third series of Marie Lu's I've read to completion, and once again, I am amazed at her talent at building complex, compelling settings and creating characters you empathize with (as well as some you root against). Sure, sometimes the plots get a little bit technical or complicated, but at their core, Lu's books are about human connection, and we can all use a little more of that.<br /><br />"When the world is murky, guide yourself with your own steady light."<br /><br />A lot has changed for Emika Chen in a short period of time. It seems like only yesterday she was on the verge of eviction from her NYC apartment, working as a bounty hunter to make ends meet. But when she accidentally hacked into the world-renowned Warcross Championships, she was summoned to Japan, where she became immersed in the virtual world of Warcross; became a celebrity in her own right; got to meet her childhood hero, Hideo Tanaka, who created Warcross; and found herself a target in a plot she didn't quite understand.<br /><br />As her relationship with Hideo grew closer, she discovered that he was using the NeuroLink algorithm not just as a way for people to get information, and as a way to harness technology for good, but he was using it for nefarious (although understandable) purposes as well. The one person she trusted more than anything has betrayed her, she's being hunted down by assassins who want her dead for somehow affecting the last Warcross Championships, and she's being courted by the dangerous and mysterious Zero and his group of anarchists.<br /><br />Although Zero had proved a threat to Emika and her friends in the past, now he wants to partner with her to accomplish what she wants—to disable the NeuroLink algorithm, which now has countless citizens in its thrall. To do so, however, means crossing Hideo, and destroying what he has spent his life building. But how much can she trust Zero and his cohorts? What effect will her actions have on her life, Hideo, her friends, and the world? She discovers the truth to be a more tangled web than even she is able to solve, and she needs to figure out whom she can trust—fast.<br /><br />If you didn't read <b>
  <i>Warcross</i>
</b>, the first book in this series (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2194872353" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">read my review</a>), the above plot summary probably reads like Greek to you, but suffice it to say, this book is just as fascinating—and perhaps ultimately richer in emotion—than its predecessor. I've tried to keep the description fairly brief because there are a lot of twists and turns and double crosses, some I saw coming, some I didn't.<br /><br />Lu's talent first shows itself in her imagery, which is so evocative at times you can almost see the book playing itself out in your mind's eye. But as you get deeper into <b>
  <i>Wildcard</i>
</b> you realize how well drawn the characters are, even those in supporting roles, like Emika's Warcross teammates, and you find yourself racing through the book, eager to know how things will unfold.<br /><br />This book didn't fully capture its predecessor's magic; there were times when the plot dragged a little or got a little too mired in complexity, but ultimately, Lu's storytelling drew me back in fairly quickly. I didn't realize this was the second of a two-book series until I was nearly done with it, which saved me from the usual dilemma of do I read it quickly or do I savor it, but I'm sad it's over, although I'm hoping Lu's next series will be related to this one.<br /><br />I know the subject matter will rule this book out for some, but if the story intrigues you, I'd encourage you to pick up <b>
  <i>Warcross</i>
</b> first, and let yourself get immersed in this world Marie Lu has created. Hopefully you'll find it as compelling and crazy a ride as I did!<br /><br />See all of my reviews at <a href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com</a>, or check out my list of the best books I read in 2017 at <a href="https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2018/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2017.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2018/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2017.html</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12186112909476519594" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14826801870230655980">I went into this one without a refresher on Warcross, but found that I didn’t quite need it.   <span id="freeText14826801870230655980" style="display:none">I went into this one without a refresher on Warcross, but found that I didn’t quite need it. It was easy to slip back into this series and I was eager to settle in and see what happened...but I wasn’t even close to being ready.<br /><br />Emika is still an awesome MC. She’s strong and loyal and I loved how she is compelled to do the right thing, no matter how dangerous. Of course there are some of the same characters from Warcross, but I won’t mention anything there.<br /><br />Plot wise, I didn’t know what to expect and I was blown away. It’s a slow delicious peel back of reveals and I was captivated the entire time. Yes, I’m being vague on purpose because spoilers.<br /><br />Overall, this series has been intriguing from the start and this ending was everything I could have wanted and a few things I didn’t know I needed.<br /><br />**Huge thanks to GP Putnam’s Sons Books for Young Readers for providing the arc free of charge** </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6712686873244478774"><a href='http://www.twirlingpages.com/2018/09/18/review-wildcard-by-marie-lu/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>this review was originally posted on twirling pages</a><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/> Wildcard was WILD. <br/><br/><a href='http://www.twirlingpages.com/2017/09/13/review-warcross-marie-lu/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Warcross</a> was one of <a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=8Kz7Mctn2SQ&t=1s' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>my favorite books of last year</a>, so i (obviously) had high hopes for Wildcard. but i was also really worried i'd be disappointed. spoiler alert: I HAD NOTHING TO FEAR (aka it was fantastic). all the things i loved about Warcross came through in the sequel, while also maintaining ~suspense~ and ~mystery~. Wildcard is definitely a darker book compared to Warcross, but it's one of the things that made me love </span>
  <span id="freeText6712686873244478774" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.twirlingpages.com/2018/09/18/review-wildcard-by-marie-lu/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">this review was originally posted on twirling pages</a><br><br><br><br><br> Wildcard was WILD. <br><br><a href="http://www.twirlingpages.com/2017/09/13/review-warcross-marie-lu/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Warcross</a> was one of <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=8Kz7Mctn2SQ&amp;t=1s" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">my favorite books of last year</a>, so i (obviously) had high hopes for Wildcard. but i was also really worried i'd be disappointed. spoiler alert: I HAD NOTHING TO FEAR (aka it was fantastic). all the things i loved about Warcross came through in the sequel, while also maintaining ~suspense~ and ~mystery~. Wildcard is definitely a darker book compared to Warcross, but it's one of the things that made me love it more. it felt like a "slytherin" type of novel (and the cover is green and black so!!!).<br><br> warning: spoilers for <a href="http://www.twirlingpages.com/2017/09/13/review-warcross-marie-lu/" rel="nofollow noopener">warcross</a>!! if you haven't read the first book, don't read the review for the second book. <br><br>we begin the novel almost directly after the end of Warcross. the big reveal makes us wonder who Zero really is and what's his story. naturally, he (and the rest of his gang) become a big part of Wildcard and I WAS HERE FOR THIS. their gang, the Blackcoats, are so ruthless and so cool. i mentioned earlier about how Wildcard is super ~dark~ but the Blackcoats are a big reason why. i loved all the new characters and their stories. although a lot of it is completely new, it ties together with Warcross really naturally. <br><br><blockquote>
<br><br>"Every locked door has a key.<br><br>
</blockquote><br><br>the parallels between Warcross and Wildcard!!!! i scream. i'm obsessed with authors who do little things with their series that tie it all together; MARIE LU PRESENTED IT WITH A BOW. i actually didn't fully realize until i went back to reread parts of Warcross, but UGH. i have a lot of feelings. but. i do wish i noticed these things the first time around. i feel like i would enjoy this duology so much more if i'd read both books in one sitting. regardless, i now officially prefer duologies to series/trilogies/standalones. they're so wonderful?? <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[i'm SPECIFICALLY talking about the very last sentence of the book. <b>"So, I have a job offer for you," I say to him. "Would you like to hear more?"</b> which – idk if you noticed – is like, <em>the first thing Hideo says to Emika??!!!?</em> I'M OVERWHELMED WITH EMOTIONS. i know there were a lot of other moments but this specifically!!!! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1537282871ra/26319546.gif" width="480" height="270" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>the one issue i have with Wildcard probably has more to do with myself than anything else. i forgot a lot of details in Warcross, which made me kind of confused while reading Wildcard. (duh) for example, a lot of the side characters and relationships were completely wiped from my brain (sorry, characters!). like i mentioned earlier, i think i would've enjoyed this book so much more if i'd read it immediately after finishing, instead of a year later. i know Mare Lu probably intended the reader to experience it that way, but she could've done a better job at refreshing my memory. (but i blame my memory!!! ugh) now i want to reread both books.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[i forgot who Tremaine and, like, ALL of the Phoenix Riders were. but i guess because of that, i read them from a new perspective? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>the thing we, as readers, are most worried for is the ending of a series. personally, i was even more worried than usual because i felt UGH about Legend's ending and didn't bother reading The Young Elites' ending (both of Marie Lu's previous series). i love her books, but am usually frustrated at her endings – mostly because of what she does to characters. PROTECT MY KIDS PLS. i don't want to spoil anything but WILDCARD IS A PERFECT CONCLUSION. it ends so cohesively!! it's so subtle and allows you to imagine a world for the characters beyond the pages!! i'm so happy with it, i could cry!!!<br><br><br>in conclusion, Warcross/Wildcard is amazing. this is one of my favorite duologies. it's action-packed, carefully complex, and fast-paced; it's been a while since a read a book in one sitting and i couldn't put this one down. i'm in love with the world and how it seems too possible. i love all the characters and their relationships (and how they diversely represent different cultures and sexualities). i'm too obsessed. <br><br><br><em>note: gallery photos belong to their respectful owners. i found them on weheartit and created <a href="https://weheartit.com/xandraaling/collections/131456831-lit-warcross" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">a mood board</a> of my loves.</em></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="6712686873244478774" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/49635633-wildcard">Quotes from Wildcard</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;And that’s when I realize that, at the end, we’d all wish for the same thing. Just a little more time.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/9540563-and-that-s-when-i-realize-that-at-the-end-we-d">65 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Every problem has a solution. But after every solution, there's a new problem to tackle, some new challenge to take on. You don't stop after you solve one thing You keep going, you find a new way and a new path, try to do better and create better. tearing something down isn't the end; doing something great, or better, something right, is. Or maybe there isn't such a thing as an end goal at all. You accomplish something, and then you shift, ready to accomplish the next. You keep solving one problem after another until you change the world.&rdquo;</span>
